Ma.ry.pray.thou.for.lu.ces.soll.

To.christ.steven.John^.child.tho.be.kind.
The days of the weke. Moralysed.
(...)
I Am sunday honorable
The heed of all the weke days
That day all thing labourable
Ought to rest / and give lawde and prays.
To our creator / that always
Uvolde have us rest after travail
Man^seruaunt / and thy be he says
And the other to thyn avail.
(...)
Monday / men ought me for to call
In which / good works ought to begin
Heryng mass / the first deed of all
Intendyng to fle deedly syn
This worldly goods truly to win
Uvith labor and true excercyse
For who of good works can not blyn
To reward / shall wyn paradyse.
(...)
I tuesday / am so named of Mars
Called of gods armypotent
I love never for to be scars
Of work but always diligent
Stryuyng against life indigent.
Being in this world. and else where
To serve our lord / with good intent
As of duty / we are bound here
(...)
Uvednesday / sothely is my name
Amyd the weke is my being
Uvher in all virtues does frame
By the means of good living
I do remember the heaven king
That was sold in my season
I do work with true meaning
Him to serve / as it is reason.
Thursda^.
I am the meryest of seven
Called thursday verily
In my time the king of heaven
Made his sowper meryly
In form of breed gave his body
To his appostles / as is plain
And than washed their fete mekely
And went to olyuet mountain.
^^^day^
Named I am devout friday.
The which cares for no delight
But to mourn / fast / deal and pray
I do set all my hole appetyte
To think on the jews despyte
How they did Christ on the tree rent
And thynkyng how I may be quyte
At the dredefull judgment.
(...)
Saturday I am coming last
Trustyng on the time spent well
Having ever mind steadfast
On that lord that harowed hell
That he my sins will expel
At the instaunce of his mother
Uvhose goodness does far excel
Uvhome I serve above all other.
The manner to live well.
The manner to ^yue well, ^e^^u^ly an^ salutarily ^ue^y day ^or all persons of
me^ (...) ^^^ate. Compyled by master Johan quu^ doctor at (...) at Paris:
trans^^ted ou^ of french in tho english by Rober^ Copland prynter at London.

FOr to begin the manner of salutary or helthfull living. And to come to
perfection (how well I have more need to be instruct than for to teache other)
yet keep these small doctri^es here following to your powers. First rise up
at.vi. of the clock in the morning in all seaso^s and in your rysyng do as
follows. Thank our lord of the rest that he gave you that night. Commend
you to god / to our blyssed lady saint mary and to that saint which is feested
that day / and to all the saints of heaven. Secondly beseech god that he
preserve the that day / from deedly sin / and at all other times. And pray
him that all the works that other does for you may be accept to the lawde of
his name / of his glorious mother / and of all the company of heaven.

Uvhan ye have arrayed you / say in your chamber or lodgyng: matyns pryme / and
hours if ye may. Than go to the church or ye do any worldly works if ye have
no needful business. and abide in the church the space of a low mass while
where ye shall think and thank god of his bn^fytes. Think a while on the
goodness of god / on his dyuyne might and virtue. Think what gift he has
given to you to create you so nobly / as to his image and likeness. Think
also what grace he has done to you in the sacrament of baptysme / clensyng
your soul from sin. Think how many times ye have offended him sith ye were
cristened. Think how mekely he has abyden your retournyng from sin. Think
from how many dangers he has preserved your body and soul. Think how ill ye
have bestowed the time that he has given you to do penance. Think how many
times she has forgyuen you in shryft / and how many times ye have fallen to
sin again. Think in what pain ye had be^ now and ever if god had taken you
out of this world when ye were i^ deedly sin. Think how derely he bought
you from the danger of the devil / suffryng co^tynuall pains in this world
/ about the space of.xxxij. years / going barefote in cold and heat /
suffryng ho^gre / and thyrst / and many shame full iniuryes and how derely he
redeemed you / gyuyng his pcious body / his blood / and his soul. and at this
point consydre all the pains of his woeful passion / as god will give you
grace. Think also what pain his dear and glorious mother suffered all that
while. Co^sydre his sharp judgment at the hour of death. And touching this
death think often thereon / and that ye can not escape it / nor knows when /
nor how / i^ what estate / nor what place / nor time day / nor hour. Think
than wat shall become of the worldly goods that ye have gadred and spared with
great labor and how loathe ye shall be to leave them and all your friends and
kynsfolke. And that more is when your soul in great pain shall leave your
body to rotte in the earth. Co^sydre than what shall become of your strength /
beauty / youth health and other welthe of the body. Think what the poor
soul shall do when it gooth alone without company where it was never. Think
what it shall do wha^ it sees the horrible enmyes that would draw it to
perdycion if ye deye in deedly sin. Think how woeful a journey it shall be
when ye must yield a general rekenyng of all your works / words / and
thoughts without excepcyo^ of any thing. Think how god shall give you grace.
Think on the horrible pains of hell / and on the cruel company of deuylles:
where without end ye shall never / have releas / if ye deye in deedly sin.
And think on the inestymable joy of the saints in heaven / the which our
lord has promised you of ye live out of deedly sin / and love him above all
thing. And have ye a perfyte hope if ye live well ye shall come to that glory.
Amen. And (...) ben ^he thoughte^ that I will that ye ha^^ ^n ^h^ ^hyrche^

And if by any other reasonable business ye may not be so long in the church
/ at it is said here before. yield thanks to god of his goodness. And think
on the resydew in your hows ones in the day or in the night if ye may.

When ye are come fro the church take heed to your household or occupacyo^
till dinner time. And in so doing think sometime that the pain that ye suffer
in this world is nothing to the regard of the i^fynyte glory that ye shall
have if ye take it mekely. Than take your refeccyon or mele reasonably without
excess or over much for beryng of your meat for there is as much danger in
to little as in to much. if ye fast ones in a weke it is enough / beside
vigilles and ymbre days out of lenten. And if ye think the fasting be not
good nor prouffytable do by council. Rest you after dinner an hour or half an
hour as ye think best / prayeng goh that in that rest he will accept your
health / to the end that after it ye may serve him the more devoutly. The
resydew of the day bestow in your business to the pleasure of god. As
touching your service say unto tiers a fore dinner. and make an end of all
before souper. And when ye may say dyryge and commendacyons for all christen
souls / at the leest way on the holy days and if ye have leaser say them on
other days / at the leest with three lessons. Shryue you every weke to your
curate except ye have great let. And beware ye pass not a fourtenyght
except very great let. if ye be of power refuse not your alms to the
first poor body that axeth it of you that day. if ye think it needful. Take
pain to here and keep the word of god. Confess you every day to god witout
fail / of such sins as ye know that ye have done that day. Co^sydre often
either by day or night when ye do awake what our lord did at that hour the
day of his blyssed passion / and where he was at that hour. Seek a good and
faithful friend of good co^uersacion to whom ye may dyscouer your mind
secrets. Enquere and prove him well or ye trust in him. And when ye have well
proved him do all by his council. Say little / and follow virtuous company.
Eschew the felaw ship of them that ye would not be like. After all work pray
se and ta^ke god / love him above all things / and serve him and his glorious
mother diligently. do to noue other but that ye would were done to you. love the
wealth of an other as your own. And in going to your bed have some good
thought either o^ the passion of our lord / or of your sins / or of the
pains that ^oules have in purgatory^ or some other good spu^all thoughts. And
th^n I hope your living shall be acceptable and pleasyng to god.

Uigilie Mortuorum.


^We have sometime abyden our chance
In this world / passing time lustely
But now ye must come trace on our dance
All adams kind be ordained to dye.


^Uve ben in glory and worldly favor
Full of all wealth / richesse / and substance
But now we perceive that come is the hour
That we must leave all lust and pleasaunce.

Oration ad deum.
COnditor celi and terre rex regu^ and dn^s domina^tiu^: qui me de nichilo
fecisti ad imagine^ and silitudine^ tua^: and me de proprio tuo sa^guine read
misti. Que^ ego pcto^r non sum dignus nominare nec i^uocare nec^ cord
cogitare. Te suppliciter depcor and hu^iliter exoro vt clementer respicias me
seruu^ tuu^ nequa^. Et miserere mei q misertus fuisti mulieri chananee and
marie magdalene / q pepercisti publicano and latroni in cruce pe^denti. Tibi
co^fiteor pater ptissime peccata mea: que si volo abscondere non possum tibi
dn^e. Parce michi christ: quia ego pauper multu^ offendi te in superbia / in
auaritia / i^gula / i^ luxuria / in vana glia / i^ odio / i^ accidia / in
adulterijs / in furto / in me^dacio / in blasphemia / in ioco / in risu / in
vbis ociosis / in auditu / in gustu / in tactu / cogitando / loque^do /
operando / and in omnibus modis in quibus ego fragilis homo and peccator
peccare potui. Mea culpa: mea culpa: mea maxi^a culpa. Ideo deprecor tuam
clementiam que de celo pro mea salute descendit: que david a peccati lapsu
erexit. Parce michi dn^e / parce michi christ: qui petro te neganti
pepercisti. Tu es creator meus and adiutor meus: plasmator meus and redemptor
meus: gubernator meus and pater meus: dn^s meus and deus meus and rex meus. Tu
es spes mea and fiducia mea: gubernatio mea and auxiliatio mea: consolatio mea
and fortitudo mea: defensio mea and liberatio mea: vita mea and salus mea et
resurrectio mea. Tu es firmamentu^ meu^ and refugiu^ meu^: lumen meu^ and
desideriu^ meu^: adiutoriu^ meu^ and patrociniu^ meu^. Te deprecor and rogo
adiuua me and saluus ero: guberna me and defend me / co^forta me and consola
me / confirma me and letifica me / illumina me and visita me. Suscipe me
mortuu^ q factura and opus tuus sum dn^e: ne despicias. Famulus et seruus tuus
sum: quamuis malus quamuis indignus and peccator. Sed qualiscu^que sim sieve
bonus sieve malus: semper tuus sum. Ad quem ergo fugiam: nisi ad te vadam? Si tu
me eijeis quis me recipiet? Si tu me despicis: quis me aspiciet? Et recognosce
me indignum ad te refugiente^ quamuis sim vilis and immundus. Quia si vilis and
immundussum potes me mundare. Si cecus sum potes me illuminare. Si infirmus sum
potes me sanare. Si mortuus and sepultus sum potes me resuscitare: q mayor est
pietas tua quam impietas mea. Plus potes dimittere quam ego co^mittere: et plus
parcere quam ego peccator peccare. Non ergo respicias dn^e neque attendas
multitudine^ iniquitatu^ mearum: sed secundu^ multitudine^ miserationu^ tuaru^
miserere mei / and propitius esto michi miserrimo peccatori. Dic ai^e me /
salus tua ego sum. Qui dixisti nolo mortem peccatoris: sed magis vt viuat et
conuertatur. convert me dn^e ad te: and noli irasci co^tra me. Deprecor te
clementissime pater propter misericordiam tuam / supplico and exoro vt perducas
me ad bonum finem: ad veram penitentiam: pura^ co^fessionem: and dignam
satisfactionem omnium peccatorum meorum. Amen.

Certain questyons.
(...)
^yrst. What is penite^ce? Penite^ce is the en^^ dacyon of the life with in
ward contricyon of heart for the sin committed: with a full purp^se never do
the sin again. ^ What is the effect of penite^ce? Penite^ce makes au^gelles
glad: iustyfyeth wicked persons: calls again the goodn^s lost: and draws
mankind unto everlasting lyf^.

How many necessary things be long to penite^ce? Five which ben they. Hope
of forgyuenes: co^tricyon of heart: co^fessyon of the fault: fulfyllyng of
such things as the priest shall command and en ^oyne: and utterly to
forsake sin. ^ How is sin avoided? By avoiding occasyo^ thereof: as is
pleasure: the beholdynge of the wa^ton plays: evil company: and such other.
Who shall never be forgyuen? He that forgyueth not to other and he that to his
power will not restore again things wrong fully taken. How prouest thou that?
For it is said in the Pr nr. Dimitte nobes debita nra: sicut and nos
dimittimus debitoribus nris. Good lord forgive us as we forgive. and saint
augustine says. No^ dimittit pctm nisi restituat ablatu^. The sin is never
forgyue^ till the thing wrongfully taken be restored. There fore when we
offend in word or in deed we ought to our power make satisfaccyon. And what
evil will / malice / or hatred we have conceived against any we should put it
out of our mind / to the^ the that our ^fessyo^ may be acceptable to god.

Uvhat is co^fessyon? Co^fessyon is the declaracy on of sin before a priest /
or any other i^ necessite.

Under what manner ought the confession be? True / of thy propre sins hole /
spedefull / often / sure manerly / volu^tarely / clear / with such delyberacyo^
that it may plainly be understand and with so great co^trycyon that it may
make the sorry: and heavy to have ^mitted those sins / fully minding never to
return to them again and so for the surely purposynge to do penance.
^Uvhat should I do willing to be confessed? Before all things in thy bed
chamber or other secret place much and often times think by thyselfe: where:
how: wha^: with: whom: how many times: and how enormely thou have sinned:
whether in speaking: co^sente: will: or deed: what good deed thou left which
thou ought to have done. Nor it is not sufficye^t to ^fesse the a liar: but
thou must hole expsse what ill has followed upon that lie. Nor thou shall not
only say. I have sinned in glotony: but thou must tell how much whether thou
were dronken: or dydest vomyte. etc. i^ what place it was: and how often. And
wha^ thou dilyge^tly by thyselfe have discussed and considered all things:
than go thou to the pest with great reverence: and not as thou would tell a
tale: and after the sin of the cross made upon ty breast say. Bndicite. Than
after a few words speken of the priest thou ^salt proceed in this manner.
Confiteor d^o celi. etc. till thou come to mea culpa. Than begynde to declare
how thou have sinned. First in thought: after in speaking: lastly in warke and
omissyon. In warke i^ the seven deedly sins / in the sins ^gaynst the holy
ghost. etc. Omissyon in the co^maundeme^te^s and warkes of mercy. etc. ^ Uvhat
is sin? There are two latin words for sin: one called pctm that other
delictu^. Peccatum: is the sin when we be dysobedie^t to the commandments
of god. Delictum: is the sin when we leave a good warke undone: the which we
ought to have done: but the difference of these two latin words are al most
confounded. How many manner of sins are there? Three. Orygynall sin of our
holy father Adam which is put always by baptym. Ue nyall ready always to be
forgyuen: also without co^fessyon. Mortal sin which without co^fessyon and
penance ledeth man to everlasting death.

How many mortal sins ben there? Seven. Pride: wrath: envy: glotony:
lechery: sloth: and couetyse. ^ Which ben the sins against the holy ghost?
Pertinacite: striuynge against trynite: because god is mercy full to sinners:
despere of the forgyuenes of god: obstynacyon in evil hatred and envy of thy
neighbors virtue: inuyde^ce: despysynge of penance. ^ Uvhiche ben sins
causyng euylles for to be done? Irritacyon / consent consell, laudacyon /
permyssion / socoure / and also perticipacyon.

Uhiche ben the sins crye^ge before god for ve^geaunce? Ma^slaughter / sin
against nature / oppressyon o poor people: and with holding of dettes ^
Which ben the circu^staunces augme^tynge sins? Order: time: science: age:
condicyon: nombre: a bydynge: abondaunce: cause: manner: dignyte: and weyke
resystence. etc.

And than begin your confession after in this manner.

The form of co^fessyon.
(...)
^yrst I knowledge myself gylty unto almighty god / unto our lady saint Mary /
and to all the company of heaven / and to you my goostly father: that sith the
time of my last confession I have offended my lord god grievously / and
specially in the.vij. deedly sins.

(...)
^ Have sinned in pride of heart / not lowly tha^ king god of gyf^es and
co^nynge which he has lent me. Also I have sinned in pride of clo^tynge: in
strength: in eloquence: in beauty: in proud words. whereof I cry god mercy.

(...)
Also I have sinned in envy: herynge any man more praised than I or better
cherysshed with his sovereign than I ^or he had more prosperyte than I / and
when I have mysanswered mine even cryste^ reioysynge. whereof I cry god mercy.

(...)
^ Also I have sinned in wrath: as in rigor of heart against mine even
christian: whether it were little matter or great and for every word I wylled to
be aue^ged on them and answered them with evil words and often smyten them.
whereof I cry god mercy.

(...)
^ Also I have sinned in slouthe^ and specially in heaviness of heart: and delyted
me in idle though^es and ymagynacyons of the world and my flesh / not
thanking god of his benefyte neither being sorry for my sins nor occupied
mys^lfe in good prayers nor holy meditacyons for the conforte o^ my soul:
whereof I cry god mercy.

(...)
^Also I have sinned in couetyse by unlawful desired of worldly goods in
misspe^dynge and unreasonably keeping of them: and I have ouermoche desired
wealth and prosperity and more worldly worshhyp and richesse than I had / and
grutched at trybulacyons / aduersyte and pouerte: whereof I cry god mercy.

(...)
^Also I have sinned in glotony by unreasonable lusts of metes and drynkes /
more for flesshely lust than for bodyly sustenau^ce / and I have done gret^
excess of metes and drynkes so that nature might not ber it whereby I was the
worse dysposed to s^rue my lord god and the more styred to sin / wrath and
wretchedness: whereof I cry god mercy.

(...)
^Also I have sinned in lechery / by foul tou^chyng by tought of fylthy lusts
and uncleanness / some time in deed done / in pollucyons and feeling of m^ own
flesh / also in sight of vyrgyns and vydo^wes. etc. whereof I cry god mercy.

(...)
^Also I have sinned in brekynge of the.x. commandments. I have not loved my
lord god about all thing nor my neighbor as my self. I hau^ customably
sworn by my lord god / by his name in vain / by his sweet body and his
saints all. I have not hallowed the feestes and holy days co^maun^ded by the
church. I have not done dew reverence to my fader and mother / nor to my
goostly fader / nor followed their techinge. I have sinned i^ backbytynge mine
even christian / in appayrynge of their good name and defylynge them with my
words. I have harmed my neygbours taking their goods against their will by
wrong. I have sinned f^lesshely with persons that been wedded and other moo
and more would if might have had time and place I have borne falls wytnes
against mine even christen. I have coueyted to have my neighbors wife /
daughter or servant and would if I had might. I have inordynatly coueyted the
goods of my neighbors contrary to the laws of god: whereof I cry god mercy.

The.v. wits.
^Ferthermore I have sinned in myspendyng of my.v. wits that is to say / in
sight of eyes / tastynge of mouth / herynge of eres / smelling of nose /
touching of hands and fete and with other me^bres of the body: whereof I cry
god mercy.

(...)
^Also I have sinned i^ not fulfyllynge of the.vij. works of mercy bodyly by
will / power and deed. I have not clothed the naked. I have not given drink to
the thyrsty. I have not ^edde the hu^gry. I have not visited the prisoners and
the seek. I have not departed of my goods to the poor. I have not harbored
the harborlesse. I have not buried the deed according to the commandments of
god: whereof I cry god mercy.

(...)
^Also I have sinned in not fulfyllyng the.vij. works of mercy spirytuall. I
have not given co^seyle to them that had need. I have not taugh the ignorant.
I have not discretly correcked the^ that had offended. I have not conforted
the^ that have been in heaviness. I have not forgyued them that have mysdone or
myssayd by me. I have not pacyently suffered them that have reproved me. I have
not devoutly prayed to god for my neighbor tot give him grace to amend his
sinful living and continue in virtue.

The (...) holy ghost.
^Also I have not used the gifts of the holy ghost to the honor of god: as
the gift of understanding: the gift of wisdom: the gift of counsel: the
gift of science: the gift of strength: the gift of pity: and the gift of
dread. whero^ I cry god mercy.

(...)
Also I have not given thanks to our lord for the.vij. sacraments. As the
sacrament of baptym: of co^firmacyon: of penance: of the body of our lord: of
wedlock of priest hode: and of enelynge. whereof being repentaunt I cry god
mercy.

(...)
Also I have not disposed me to the.viij. beatitudes: as pouerte of spirit:
perfyte mekenes i^ aduersyte: perfyte mekenes in prosperyte: lust of right
wysnesse: perfyte mercy: clennesse of heart: peace in desire joyful suffraunce
of persecucyon in the cause of virtue. whereof I cry god mercy.

Of these and all other: known and not known that ever I did sith I was
borne unto this day I ask god mercy: and most merciful lord god I yield me
gylty unto the and utterly put me unto thy grace / pity / and mercy: and I
pray you my goostly fa^er to be bettwene my sin and me that god of his mercy
forgive me for this lowely co^fessyon that I may be free fro my goostly ennemy
and optayn the endless bliss that god has bought me to I deo deprecor. etc.
